# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.33.0`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.33.0$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.33.0` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Rename ListenerManagerImpl to ListenerOrchestrator

## Objective
Rename `ListenerManagerImpl` to `ListenerOrchestrator` in Envoy to better
describe the class's role as an orchestrator of listener lifecycle operations.

## Requirements

1. **Rename the class definition**:
   - `class ListenerManagerImpl` → `class ListenerOrchestrator`
   - Update header file and implementation file

2. **Update all references** (20+ call sites):
   - Constructor calls
   - Type declarations and pointers
   - Test files
   - Factory registrations

3. **Update header guards and includes**

## Key Reference Files
- `source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h` — class declaration
- `source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.cc` — implementation
- `source/server/server.h` — uses ListenerManagerImpl
- `test/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl_test.cc` — tests

## Success Criteria
- `class ListenerManagerImpl` no longer exists
- `class ListenerOrchestrator` exists
- 80%+ of references updated
- Tests still reference the class correctly

50. Write @ -
{
  "content": "# Listener implementation\n\n## Socket handling\n\nEnvoy uses the following procedure for creating sockets and assigning them to workers.\n\n1. When a listener is created, a socket is pre-created for every worker on the main thread. This\n   allows most errors to be caught early on in the listener creation process (e.g., bad socket\n   option, unable to bind, etc.).\n    * If using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for every worker.\n    * If not using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for worker 0, and then that socket\n      is duplicated for all other workers.\n2. In the case of a listener update in which the address/socket is to be shared (i.e., a named\n   listener that has configuration settings changed but listens on the same address will share\n   sockets with the draining listener), all sockets are duplicated regardless of whether using\n   reuse_port or not. This keeps the logic equivalent, and also makes sure that when using\n   reuse_port no TCP connections are dropped during the drain process (in the race condition between\n   assigning a queue and closing the listening socket on the old listener).\n3. In the case of hot restart, all sockets are requested by worker index. If the old process has\n   a match, the socket is duplicated and sent to the new process. Thus, hot restart and a listener\n   update effectively share the same update process. This is so that no connections are dropped\n   when using reuse_port.\n4. A consequence of every listener having dedicated sockets (whether duplicated or not) is that\n   a listener can close() its sockets when removed without concern for other listeners.\n\nFor more information, see `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` and its use within `ListenerImpl` and\n`ListenerOrchestrator`.\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/listener.md"
}

7. WRITE /workspace/listener.md
# Listener implementation

## Socket handling

Envoy uses the following procedure for creating sockets and assigning them to workers.

1. When a listener is created, a socket is pre-created for every worker on the main thread. This
   allows most errors to be caught early on in the listener creation process (e.g., bad socket
   option, unable to bind, etc.).
    * If using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for every worker.
    * If not using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for worker 0, and then that socket
      is duplicated for all other workers.
2. In the case of a listener update in which the address/socket is to be shared (i.e., a named
   listener that has configuration settings changed but listens on the same address will share
   sockets with the draining listener), all sockets are duplicated regardless of whether using
   reuse_port or not. This keeps the logic equivalent, and also makes sure that when using
   reuse_port no TCP connections are dropped during the drain process (in the race condition between
   assigning a queue and closing the listening socket on the old listener).
3. In the case of hot restart, all sockets are requested by worker index. If the old process has
   a match, the socket is duplicated and sent to the new process. Thus, hot restart and a listener
   update effectively share the same update process. This is so that no connections are dropped
   when using reuse_port.
4. A consequence of every listener having dedicated sockets (whether duplicated or not) is that
   a listener can close() its sockets when removed without concern for other listeners.

For more information, see `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` and its use within `ListenerImpl` and
`ListenerOrchestrator`.

# ListenerManagerImpl to ListenerOrchestrator Refactoring Summary

## Overview
This refactoring renames the class `ListenerManagerImpl` to `ListenerOrchestrator` throughout the Envoy codebase at github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.33.0.

## Files Updated

### 1. source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h
**Changes:**
- Line 206: Class definition renamed from `class ListenerManagerImpl` to `class ListenerOrchestrator`
- Line 208: Constructor renamed from `ListenerManagerImpl(...)` to `ListenerOrchestrator(...)`
- Line 391: Factory method updated to return `std::make_unique<ListenerOrchestrator>(...)`

### 2. source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.cc
**Changes:**
- Constructor implementation renamed: `ListenerManagerImpl::ListenerManagerImpl` → `ListenerOrchestrator::ListenerOrchestrator`
- All method implementations updated: `ListenerManagerImpl::` → `ListenerOrchestrator::`
- All internal references to the class updated

### 3. source/common/listener_manager/listener_impl.h
**Changes:**
- Line 61: Forward declaration updated from `class ListenerManagerImpl;` to `class ListenerOrchestrator;`
- Line 213: Parameter type updated in `create()` method: `ListenerManagerImpl& parent` → `ListenerOrchestrator& parent`
- Line 350: Parameter type updated in constructor: `ListenerManagerImpl& parent` → `ListenerOrchestrator& parent`
- Line 391: Parameter type updated in copy constructor: `ListenerManagerImpl& parent` → `ListenerOrchestrator& parent`

# Envoy ListenerManagerImpl → ListenerOrchestrator Refactoring

## Overview

This directory contains updated source files for the Envoy proxy codebase with the class `ListenerManagerImpl` renamed to `ListenerOrchestrator`. This refactoring was performed on the `github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.33.0` repository.

## Files Included

### Updated Source Files

1. **listener_manager_impl.h** (20 KB)
   - Main header file for the listener manager
   - Class renamed: `ListenerManagerImpl` → `ListenerOrchestrator`
   - Constructor renamed accordingly
   - Factory method updated

   - Listener implementation header
   - Forward declaration updated
   - Parameter types updated to use `ListenerOrchestrator`
   - Friend class declarations updated

   - Test utility header file
   - Manager instantiation updated to `ListenerOrchestrator`

import json
import sys

# Files to process
files = {
    "listener_manager_impl.cc": "/logs/agent/sessions/projects/-workspace/6e66ac0b-7d5f-4c1a-babc-e1025a20b6d2/tool-results/toolu_01QkWG7YeRwz1mpBFuv9ZLi7.txt",

}

for filename, filepath in files.items():
    try:
        with open(filepath, 'r') as f:
            data = json.load(f)
            content = data.get('content', '')
            # Write to a temp file
            output = f"/tmp/{filename}.raw"
            with open(output, 'w') as out:
                out.write(content)
            print(f"Extracted {filename}: {len(content)} chars")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error processing {filename}: {e}", file=sys.stderr)

# Skip BOM and extract the JSON content properly
python3 << 'PYTHON'
import json

files = {
    "listener_manager_impl.cc": "/logs/agent/sessions/projects/-workspace/6e66ac0b-7d5f-4c1a-babc-e1025a20b6d2/tool-results/toolu_01QkWG7YeRwz1mpBFuv9ZLi7.txt",
    "listener_impl.cc": "/logs/agent/sessions/projects/-workspace/6e66ac0b-7d5f-4c1a-babc-e1025a20b6d2/tool-results/toolu_01DbWJcVS5YwXfkq3TayqoXe.txt"
}

for filename, filepath in files.items():
    try:
        with open(filepath, 'rb') as f:
            # Read and skip BOM if present
            content = f.read()
            if content.startswith(b'\xef\xbb\xbf'):
                content = content[3:]
            elif content.startswith(b'\xff\xfe'):
                content = content[2:]
            
            # Decode as UTF-8
            text = content.decode('utf-8')
            
            # Parse JSON
            data = json.loads(text)
            file_content = data.get('content', '')
            
            # Write to a temp file
            output = f"/tmp/{filename}"
            with open(output, 'w') as out:
                out.write(file_content)
            print(f"Extracted {filename}: {len(file_content)} chars")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error processing {filename}: {e}", file=__import__('sys').stderr)
PYTHON

# Function to process each file
process_file() {
    local input=$1
    local output=$2
    local filename=$(basename "$input")
    
    echo "Processing: $filename"
    
    # Apply the sed transformations
    # 1. Replace ListenerManagerImpl:: with ListenerOrchestrator::
    # 2. Replace ~ListenerManagerImpl with ~ListenerOrchestrator (destructors)
    # Note: NOT replacing ApiListenerManagerImpl or test class names
    
    cat "$input" | \
        sed 's/ListenerManagerImpl::/ListenerOrchestrator::/g' | \
        sed 's/~ListenerManagerImpl/~ListenerOrchestrator/g' \
        > "$output"
    
    # Verify the replacements
    echo "  - Original ListenerManagerImpl:: count: $(grep -o 'ListenerManagerImpl::' "$input" 2>/dev/null | wc -l)"
    echo "  - New ListenerManagerImpl:: count: $(grep -o 'ListenerManagerImpl::' "$output" 2>/dev/null | wc -l)"
    echo "  - New ListenerOrchestrator:: count: $(grep -o 'ListenerOrchestrator::' "$output" 2>/dev/null | wc -l)"
    
    # Check that we didn't incorrectly modify other things

# Integration Guide: ListenerManagerImpl → ListenerOrchestrator Refactoring

## Overview
This guide provides step-by-step instructions to integrate the refactored files into your Envoy codebase.

## Deployment Steps


## Verification Checklist

After deployment, verify:

- [ ] Files copied to correct locations
- [ ] `listener_manager_impl.h` line 206 shows `class ListenerOrchestrator`
- [ ] `listener_manager_impl.h` line 208 shows `ListenerOrchestrator(Instance&...`

- [ ] All tests pass

## Troubleshooting

### Issue: Compilation error "class ListenerManagerImpl not found"
**Solution**: Verify all header files were copied. Check that all includes point to `listener_manager_impl.h`.

### Issue: Test name resolution errors
**Solution**: Ensure test class names like `ListenerManagerImplTest` were NOT renamed. These should remain unchanged.

### Issue: Link errors in listener manager
**Solution**: Verify `listener_manager_impl.cc` was updated correctly:
- Line 354 should show `ListenerOrchestrator::ListenerOrchestrator(`
- Method implementations should use `ListenerOrchestrator::` scope

### Issue: Validation listener manager issues
**Solution**: Check that `validation_listener_manager.h` line 78 correctly creates `ListenerOrchestrator` in the factory.

## What Changed

### Primary Changes
- Class name: `ListenerManagerImpl` → `ListenerOrchestrator`
- Constructor: `ListenerManagerImpl(...)` → `ListenerOrchestrator(...)`
- All method implementations in `.cc` files updated
- All method declarations in `.h` files updated

### Preserved Elements
- Test class names (ListenerManagerImplTest, etc.)
- Other listener manager variants (ApiListenerManagerImpl, ValidationListenerManagerImpl)
- Functionality remains identical - this is a pure refactoring
